       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Geography of the United Arab Emirates">Geography of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png/290px-United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png/435px-United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png/580px-United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="1967" data-file-height="1730"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:United_Arab_Emirates_Topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topography of the UAE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Arab Emirates is situated in Middle East, bordering the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman" title="Gulf of Oman">Gulf of Oman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, between Oman and Saudi Arabia; it is in a strategic location slightly south of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">Strait of Hormuz</a>, a vital transit point for world <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">crude oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE lies between 22°30' and 26°10' north latitude and between 51° and 56°25′ east longitude. It shares a 530-kilometre (330&nbsp;mi) border with Saudi Arabia on the west, south, and southeast, and a 450-kilometre (280&nbsp;mi) border with Oman on the southeast and northeast. The land border with Qatar in the <a href="/wiki/Khawr_al_Udayd" title="Khawr al Udayd">Khawr al Udayd</a> area is about nineteen kilometres (12 miles) in the northwest; however, it is a source of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_%E2%80%93_United_Arab_Emirates_border_dispute" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi Arabia – United Arab Emirates border dispute">ongoing dispute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Following Britain's military departure from the UAE in 1971, and its establishment as a new state, the UAE laid claim to islands resulting in disputes with Iran that remain unresolved. The UAE also disputes claim on other islands against the neighboring state of Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The largest emirate, <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_(emirate)" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Dhabi (emirate)">Abu Dhabi</a>, accounts for 87% of the UAE's total area<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> (67,340 square kilometres (26,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The smallest emirate, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Ajman" title="Emirate of Ajman">Ajman</a>, encompasses only 259&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (100&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)(see figure).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg/220px-Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg/330px-Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg/440px-Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_United_Arab_Emirates_in_October.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite image of United Arab Emirates
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE coast stretches for nearly 650&nbsp;km (404&nbsp;mi) along the southern shore of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, briefly interrupted by an isolated outcrop of the Sultanate of Oman. Six of the emirates are on situated along the Persian Gulf, and the seventh, Fujairah is on the eastern coast of the peninsula with direct access to the Gulf of Oman.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Most of the coast consists of <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt pans</a> that extend 8–10&nbsp;km inland.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The largest <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">natural harbor</a> is at Dubai, although other ports have been dredged at Abu Dhabi, Sharjah, and elsewhere. Numerous islands are found in the Persian Gulf, and the ownership of some of them has been the subject of international disputes with both Iran and Qatar. The smaller islands, as well as many <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and shifting sandbars, are a menace to navigation. Strong tides and occasional windstorms further complicate ship movements near the shore. The UAE also has a stretch of the <a href="/wiki/Al_Batinah_Region" title="Al Batinah Region">Al Bāţinah</a> coast of the Gulf of Oman, although the <a href="/wiki/Musandam_Governorate" title="Musandam Governorate">Musandam Peninsula</a>, the very tip of Arabia by the Strait of Hormuz, is an <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a> of Oman separated by the UAE.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Jebel_Jais_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roads leading to <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Jais" title="Jebel Jais">Jebel Jais</a>, the highest mountain in the UAE (1,892 m), in <a href="/wiki/Ras_Al_Khaimah" title="Ras Al Khaimah">Ras Al Khaimah</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South and west of Abu Dhabi, vast, rolling <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">sand dunes</a> merge into the Rub al-Khali (Empty Quarter) of Saudi Arabia. The desert area of Abu Dhabi includes two important oases with adequate underground water for permanent settlements and cultivation. The extensive <a href="/wiki/Liwa_Oasis" title="Liwa Oasis">Liwa Oasis</a> is in the south near the undefined border with Saudi Arabia. About 100&nbsp;km (62&nbsp;mi) to the northeast of Liwa is the <a href="/wiki/Al_Buraimi_Governorate" title="Al Buraimi Governorate">Al-Buraimi</a> oasis, which extends on both sides of the Abu Dhabi-Oman border. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Zakher" title="Lake Zakher">Lake Zakher</a> in Al Ain is a <a href="/wiki/Man-made_lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Man-made lake">human-made lake</a> near the border with Oman that was created from treated waste water.<sup id="cite_ref-Man-made_desert_lake:_Ecological_paradise_or_disaster?_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Man-made_desert_lake:_Ecological_paradise_or_disaster?-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to withdrawing from the area in 1971, Britain delineated the internal borders among the seven emirates in order to preempt territorial disputes that might hamper formation of the federation. In general, the rulers of the emirates accepted the British interventions, but in the case of boundary disputes between Abu Dhabi and Dubai, and also between Dubai and Sharjah, conflicting claims were not resolved until after the UAE became independent. The most complicated borders were in the <a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_Mountains" title="Al Hajar Mountains">Al-Hajar al-Gharbi</a> Mountains, where five of the emirates contested jurisdiction over more than a dozen enclaves. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Wildlife of the United Arab Emirates">Wildlife of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg/220px-1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg/330px-1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg/440px-1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1501200713074_Acacia_tortilis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">Acacia</a> trees growing in desert suburbs near <a href="/wiki/Fujairah" title="Fujairah">Fujairah</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE contains four terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_montane_woodlands" title="Al Hajar montane woodlands">Al Hajar montane woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman_desert_and_semi-desert" title="Gulf of Oman desert and semi-desert">Gulf of Oman desert and semi-desert</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al-Hajar_foothill_xeric_woodlands_and_shrublands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al-Hajar foothill xeric woodlands and shrublands (page does not exist)">Al-Hajar foothill xeric woodlands and shrublands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al-Hajar_montane_woodlands_and_shrublands" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Hajar montane woodlands and shrublands">Al-Hajar montane woodlands and shrublands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The oases grow <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix dactylifera">date palms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> trees. In the desert, the flora is very sparse and consists of <a href="/wiki/Grasses" class="mw-redirect" title="Grasses">grasses</a> and thorn bushes. The indigenous fauna had come close to extinction because of intensive hunting, which has led to a conservation program on <a href="/wiki/Sir_Bani_Yas" title="Sir Bani Yas">Sir Bani Yas</a> Island initiated by Sheikh Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan in the 1970s, resulting in the survival of, for example, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Oryx" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabian Oryx">Arabian Oryx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_camel" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabian camel">Arabian camel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>. <a href="/wiki/Coastal_fish" title="Coastal fish">Coastal fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammals">mammals</a> consist mainly of <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">mackerel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estuary_perch" title="Estuary perch">perch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">sharks</a> and whales. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <p>The climate of the UAE is subtropical-arid with hot summers and warm winters. The climate is categorized as desert climate. The hottest months are July and August, when average maximum temperatures reach above 45&nbsp;°C (113&nbsp;°F) on the <a href="/wiki/Coastal_plain" title="Coastal plain">coastal plain</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_Mountains" title="Al Hajar Mountains">Al Hajar Mountains</a>, temperatures are considerably lower, a result of increased elevation.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Average minimum temperatures in January and February are between 10 and 14&nbsp;°C (50 and 57&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> During the late summer months, a humid southeastern wind known as Sharqi (i.e. "Easterner") makes the coastal region especially unpleasant. The average annual rainfall in the coastal area is less than 120&nbsp;mm (4.7&nbsp;in), but in some mountainous areas annual rainfall often reaches 350&nbsp;mm (13.8&nbsp;in). Rain in the coastal region falls in short, torrential bursts during the summer months, sometimes resulting in floods in ordinarily dry <a href="/wiki/Wadi" title="Wadi">wadi</a> beds.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The region is prone to occasional, violent <a href="/wiki/Dust_storm" title="Dust storm">dust storms</a>, which can severely reduce visibility. </p>
      <p>On 28 December 2004, there was snow recorded in the UAE for the first time, in the <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Jais" title="Jebel Jais">Jebel Jais</a> mountain cluster in Ras al-Khaimah.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> A few years later, there were more sightings of snow and hail.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The Jebel Jais mountain cluster has experienced snow only twice since records began.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Politics of the United Arab Emirates">Politics of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Arab Emirates is a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> made up from a federation of seven <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditary</a> tribal <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">monarchy</a>-styled political system called <a href="/wiki/Sheikhdoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikhdoms">Sheikhdoms</a>. It is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Council" title="Federal Supreme Council">Federal Supreme Council</a> made up of the ruling Sheikhs of <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_(emirate)" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Dhabi (emirate)">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Ajman" title="Emirate of Ajman">Ajman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Fujairah" title="Emirate of Fujairah">Fujairah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_(emirate)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah (emirate)">Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Dubai" title="Emirate of Dubai">Dubai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ras_al-Khaimah" class="mw-redirect" title="Ras al-Khaimah">Ras al-Khaimah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umm_al-Quwain" class="mw-redirect" title="Umm al-Quwain">Umm al-Quwain</a>. All responsibilities not granted to the national government are reserved to the individual emirate.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> A percentage of revenues from each emirate is allocated to the UAE's central budget.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The United Arab Emirates uses the title <a href="/wiki/Sheikh" title="Sheikh">Sheikh</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">Emir</a> to refer to the rulers of individual emirates. The title is used due to the sheikhdom styled governing system in adherence to the culture of <a href="/wiki/Tribes_of_Arabia" title="Tribes of Arabia">tribes of Arabia</a>, where Sheikh means leader, elder, or the tribal chief of the clan who partakes in shared decision making with his followers. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="President of the United Arab Emirates">President</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of the United Arab Emirates">Prime Minister</a> are elected by the Federal Supreme Council. Usually, a sheikh from Abu Dhabi holds the presidency and a sheikh from Dubai the prime minister-ship. All prime ministers but one have served concurrently as vice president. Sheikh Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan is the UAE founding father and widely accredited for unifying the seven emirates into one country. He was the UAE's first president from the nation's founding until his death on 2 November 2004. On the following day the Federal Supreme Council elected his son, <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Sheikh Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a>, to the post.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The federal government is composed of three branches: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative</a>: A <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Council" title="Federal Supreme Council">Federal Supreme Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Advisory_board" title="Advisory board">advisory</a> <a href="/wiki/Federal_National_Council" title="Federal National Council">Federal National Council</a> (FNC).</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">Executive</a>: The <a href="/wiki/President_of_UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="President of UAE">President</a>, who is also <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the military, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of the United Arab Emirates">Prime Minister</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Cabinet of the United Arab Emirates">Council of Ministers</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judicial</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Federal Supreme Court of the United Arab Emirates">Supreme Court</a> and lower federal courts.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/E-Government_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="E-Government in the United Arab Emirates">UAE e-Government</a> is the extension of the UAE Federal Government in its electronic form.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The UAE's <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Cabinet of the United Arab Emirates">Council of Ministers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">مجلس الوزراء</span>‎) is the chief executive branch of the government presided over by the Prime Minister. The Prime Minister, who is appointed by the Federal Supreme Council, appoints the ministers. The Council of Ministers is made up of 22 members and manages all internal and foreign affairs of the federation under its constitutional and federal law.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The UAE is the only country in the world that has a Ministry of Tolerance,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> a Ministry of Happiness,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and a Ministry of Artificial Intelligence.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The UAE also has a virtual ministry called the Ministry of Possibilities, designed to find solutions to challenges and improve quality of life.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The UAE also has a <a href="/wiki/National_Youth_Council" title="National Youth Council">National Youth Council</a>, which is represented in the UAE cabinet by the Minister of Youth.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE legislative is the <a href="/wiki/Federal_National_Council" title="Federal National Council">Federal National Council</a> which convenes nationwide elections every 4 years. The FNC consists of 40 members drawn from all the emirates. Each emirate is allocated specific seats to ensure full representation. Half are appointed by the rulers of the constituent emirates, and the other half are elected. By law, the council members have to be equally divided between males and females. The FNC is restricted to a largely <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/consultation" class="extiw" title="wikt:consultation">consultative</a> role.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE is described by western observers as an "<a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocracy</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, the UAE is "an autocracy with the sheen of a progressive, modern state".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The UAE ranks poorly in <a href="/wiki/Freedom_indices" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom indices">freedom indices</a> measuring <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Political rights">political rights</a>. The UAE is annually ranked as "Not Free" in Freedom House's annual <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> report, which measures civil liberties and political rights.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Arab_Emirates_Reports_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Arab_Emirates_Reports-117">[117]</a></sup> The UAE also ranks poorly in the annual <a href="/wiki/Reporters_without_Borders" class="mw-redirect" title="Reporters without Borders">Reporters without Borders</a>' <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a>. </p>
      <p>Sheikh Zayed was asked by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> in April 1997 on why there is no elected <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> in the United Arab Emirates, in which he replied: </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>Why should we abandon a system that satisfies our people, in order to introduce a system that seems to engender <a href="/wiki/Dissent" title="Dissent">dissent</a> and confrontation? Our system of government is based upon our religion and that is what our people want. Should they seek alternatives, we are ready to listen to them. We have always said that our people should voice their demands openly. We are all in the same boat, and they are both the captain and the crew. Our doors are open for any opinion to be expressed, and this is well known by all our citizens. It is our deep conviction that God has created people free, and has prescribed that each individual must enjoy <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_choice" title="Freedom of choice">freedom of choice</a>. No one should act as if they own others.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Foreign relations of the United Arab Emirates">Foreign relations of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_(41210385295).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%2841210385295%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%2841210385295%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%2841210385295%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%2841210385295%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%2841210385295%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%2841210385295%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4339" data-file-height="3384"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Shakes_Hands_With_UAE_Foreign_Minister_Sheikh_Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_(41210385295).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Minister of Foreign Affairs <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Abdullah bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Abdullah bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a>, 2018.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE has extensive diplomatic and commercial relations with other countries. It plays a significant role in <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> and the UN, and is one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> (GCC). One of the main anchorers of the UAE's foreign policy has been building cooperation-based relations with all countries of the world. Substantial development assistance has increased the UAE's stature among recipient states. Most of this foreign aid (in excess of $15 billion) has been to Arab and Muslim countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and several of its specialized agencies (<a href="/wiki/ICAO" class="mw-redirect" title="ICAO">ICAO</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">ILO</a>, <a href="/wiki/UPU" class="mw-redirect" title="UPU">UPU</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a>, <a href="/wiki/WIPO" class="mw-redirect" title="WIPO">WIPO</a>), as well as the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC), OPEC, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Arab_Petroleum_Exporting_Countries" title="Organization of Arab Petroleum Exporting Countries">Organization of Arab Petroleum Exporting Countries</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Also, it is an observer in the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_Internationale_de_la_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie</a>. </p>
      <p>The UAE maintains close relations with <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and is Egypt's largest investor from the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Pakistan was the first country to formally recognize the UAE upon its formation and continues to be one of its major economic and trading partners.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_Arab_Emirates_relations" title="China–United Arab Emirates relations">China and UAE</a> are also strong international allies, with significant cooperation across economic, political and cultural lines.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The largest expatriate presence in the UAE is <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Following the British withdrawal from the UAE in 1971 and the establishment of the UAE as a state, the UAE disputed rights to three islands in the Persian Gulf against Iran, namely <a href="/wiki/Abu_Musa" title="Abu Musa">Abu Musa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tunb" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Tunb">Greater Tunb</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Tunb" class="mw-redirect" title="Lesser Tunb">Lesser Tunb</a>. The UAE tried to bring the matter to the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>, but Iran dismissed the notion.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The dispute has not significantly impacted relations because of the large Iranian community presence and strong economic ties.<sup id="cite_ref-uaeinteract1_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uaeinteract1-128">[128]</a></sup> The UAE also has a long and a close relationship with the UK and Germany, and many European nationals reside in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Former British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> serves as a funded adviser to the <a href="/wiki/Mubadala_Development_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Mubadala Development Company">Mubadala Development Company</a>, a wholly owned investment vehicle of the government of Abu Dhabi.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Donald_Trump_meet_with_His_Highness_Sheikh_Mohamed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan,_Crown_Prince_of_Abu_Dhabi,_in_the_Oval_Office_of_the_White_House,_Monday,_May_15,_2017_(02).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Donald_Trump_meet_with_His_Highness_Sheikh_Mohamed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan%2C_Crown_Prince_of_Abu_Dhabi%2C_in_the_Oval_Office_of_the_White_House%2C_Monday%2C_May_15%2C_2017_%2802%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Donald_Trump_meet_with_His_Highness_Sheikh_Mohamed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan%2C_Crown_Prince_of_Abu_Dhabi%2C_in_the_Oval_Office_of_the_White_House%2C_Monday%2C_May_15%2C_2017_%2802%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Donald_Trump_meet_with_His_Highness_Sheikh_Mohamed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan%2C_Crown_Prince_of_Abu_Dhabi%2C_in_the_Oval_Office_of_the_White_House%2C_Monday%2C_May_15%2C_2017_%2802%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Donald_Trump_meet_with_His_Highness_Sheikh_Mohamed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan,_Crown_Prince_of_Abu_Dhabi,_in_the_Oval_Office_of_the_White_House,_Monday,_May_15,_2017_(02).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Mohammed bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> and U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> in Washington DC, May 2017.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Arab Emirates and the United States enjoy very close strategic ties. The UAE has been described as the United States' best counter-terrorism ally in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian gulf">Gulf</a> by <a href="/wiki/Richard_A._Clarke" title="Richard A. Clarke">Richard A. Clarke</a>, the US national security advisor and counter-terrorism expert.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The US maintains three military bases in the UAE. The UAE is also the only country in the Middle East which has a <a href="/wiki/United_States_border_preclearance" title="United States border preclearance">US border preclearance</a> that is staffed and operated by <a href="/wiki/US_Customs_and_Border_Protection" class="mw-redirect" title="US Customs and Border Protection">US Customs and Border Protection</a> officers, allowing travelers to reach the US as domestic travelers. In 2013, The UAE spent more than any other country in the world <a href="/wiki/Lobbying_in_the_United_States" title="Lobbying in the United States">to influence</a> <a href="/wiki/U.S._policy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. policy">U.S. policy</a> and shape domestic debate.<sup id="cite_ref-sunlightfoundation.com_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunlightfoundation.com-133">[133]</a></sup> In its dispute with the United States, Iran has repeatedly threatened to close the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">Strait of Hormuz</a>, a vital oil-trade route.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-18">[18]</a></sup> Therefore, in July 2012, the UAE began operating a key overland oil pipeline, the <a href="/wiki/Habshan%E2%80%93Fujairah_oil_pipeline" title="Habshan–Fujairah oil pipeline">Habshan–Fujairah oil pipeline</a>, which bypasses the Strait of Hormuz in order to mitigate any consequences of an Iranian shut-off. </p>
      <p>It was reported in 2019 that UAE's National Electronic Security Authority (NESA) has enlisted the help of American and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> experts in its targeting of political leaders, activists and the governments of <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>. According to <i>Reuters</i> their surveillance activities have also targeted American citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE was one of only three countries to recognise the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> as Afghanistan's legitimate government (Pakistan and Saudi Arabia were the other two countries).<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> At the encouragement of the United States, the UAE attempted to host a Taliban embassy under three conditions, which include: denouncing Al Qaeda leader Osama bin Laden, recognizing the Afghan constitution, and renouncing violence and laying down their weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-UAET_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UAET-136">[136]</a></sup> The Taliban refused all three conditions, and the UAE withdrew its offer.<sup id="cite_ref-UAET_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UAET-136">[136]</a></sup> The UAE rescinded diplomatic relations with the Taliban after <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September attacks</a> in 2001 (alongside Pakistan). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_(2019-10-15)_41.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%282019-10-15%29_41.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%282019-10-15%29_41.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%282019-10-15%29_41.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%282019-10-15%29_41.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%282019-10-15%29_41.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_%282019-10-15%29_41.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Mohammed_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan_(2019-10-15)_41.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> meeting with Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Zayed" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed bin Zayed">Mohammed bin Zayed</a> in Abu Dhabi in October 2019.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE has been actively involved in <a href="/wiki/Saudi-led_intervention_in_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi-led intervention in Yemen</a> and has supported Yemen's internationally recognized government as well as the separatist <a href="/wiki/Southern_Transitional_Council" title="Southern Transitional Council">Southern Transitional Council</a> in Yemen against the <a href="/wiki/Houthi_takeover_in_Yemen" title="Houthi takeover in Yemen">Houthi takeover in Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The Saudi-led coalition has been repeatedly accused of conducting indiscriminate and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations_during_the_Yemeni_Civil_War_(2015%E2%80%93present)" title="Human rights violations during the Yemeni Civil War (2015–present)">unlawful airstrikes on civilian targets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> became close allies when <a href="/wiki/Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud" class="mw-redirect" title="Salman bin Abdulaziz Al Saud">Salman bin Abdulaziz Al Saud</a> became King of Saudi Arabia in 2015 and <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Salman" title="Mohammed bin Salman">Mohammed bin Salman</a> as Crown Prince in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In June 2017, the UAE alongside multiple Middle Eastern and African countries cut diplomatic ties with <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> due to allegations of <a href="/wiki/Qatar_and_state-sponsored_terrorism" title="Qatar and state-sponsored terrorism">Qatar being a state sponsor of terrorism</a>, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_diplomatic_crisis" title="Qatar diplomatic crisis">Qatar diplomatic crisis</a>. The UAE backed Saudi Arabia in its <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_relations#August_2018_diplomatic_dispute" title="Canada–Saudi Arabia relations">2018 dispute with Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The UAE also backed Saudi Arabia's statement about the death of Saudi journalist <a href="/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi" title="Jamal Khashoggi">Jamal Khashoggi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> was the first pope to visit the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> on a trip to <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> in 2019 and held papal mass to more than 120,000 attendees in the <a href="/wiki/Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium" title="Zayed Sports City Stadium">Zayed Sports City Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the successful foreign policy of the UAE, the <a href="/wiki/Emirati_passport" title="Emirati passport">Emirati passport</a> became the largest individual climber in <a href="/wiki/Henley_%26_Partners_Passport_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Henley &amp; Partners Passport Index">Henley &amp; Partners Passport Index</a> in 2018 over the past decade, increasing its global rank by 28 places.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> According to the Henley Passport Index, as of 28 March 2019, Emirati citizens had visa-free or visa on arrival access to 165 countries and territories, ranking the Emirati passport 21st in the world in terms of travel freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2020, the UAE and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> reached a historic <a href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_Arab_Emirates_peace_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Israel–United Arab Emirates peace agreement">Israel–United Arab Emirates peace agreement</a> to lead towards full normalization of relations between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The agreement formally became part of the <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Accords" title="Abraham Accords">Abraham Accords</a> involving the UAE and Israel and was signed on 15 September 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The agreement came as a result of Emirati efforts to halt Israel's planned annexation of parts of the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_Armed_Forces" title="United Arab Emirates Armed Forces">United Arab Emirates Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:F-16e_block60.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/F-16e_block60.jpg/220px-F-16e_block60.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/F-16e_block60.jpg/330px-F-16e_block60.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/F-16e_block60.jpg/440px-F-16e_block60.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1123" data-file-height="807"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:F-16e_block60.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_Air_Force" title="United Arab Emirates Air Force">United Arab Emirates Air Force</a> F-16 Block 60 "<a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon_variants#F-16E/F_Block_60" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon variants">Desert Falcon</a>", taking off from the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a> plant in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Arab Emirates military force was formed in 1971 from the historical <a href="/wiki/Trucial_Oman_Scouts" title="Trucial Oman Scouts">Trucial Oman Scouts</a>, a long symbol of public order in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Arabia" title="Eastern Arabia">Eastern Arabia</a> and commanded by British officers. The Trucial Oman Scouts were turned over to the United Arab Emirates, as the nucleus of its defence forces in 1971, with the formation of the UAE, and was absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/Union_Defence_Force_(UAE)" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Defence Force (UAE)">Union Defence Force</a>. </p>
      <p>Although initially small in number, the UAE armed forces have grown significantly over the years and are presently equipped with some of the most modern weapon systems, purchased from a variety of western military advanced countries, mainly France, the US and the UK. Most officers are graduates of the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_Sandhurst" title="Royal Military Academy Sandhurst">Royal Military Academy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sandhurst,_Berkshire" title="Sandhurst, Berkshire">Sandhurst</a>, with others having attended the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">United States Military Academy</a> at <a href="/wiki/West_Point,_New_York" title="West Point, New York">West Point</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_College,_Duntroon" title="Royal Military College, Duntroon">Royal Military College, Duntroon</a> in Australia, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_sp%C3%A9ciale_militaire_de_Saint-Cyr" title="École spéciale militaire de Saint-Cyr">St Cyr</a>, the military academy of France. France and the United States have played the most strategically significant roles with defence cooperation agreements and military material provision.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some of the UAE military deployments include an infantry battalion to the United Nations <a href="/wiki/UNOSOM_II" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOSOM II">UNOSOM II</a> force in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> in 1993, the 35th Mechanised Infantry Battalion to <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, a regiment to Kuwait during the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demining" title="Demining">demining</a> operations in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Enduring_Freedom" title="Operation Enduring Freedom">Operation Enduring Freedom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">American-led intervention in Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/American-led_intervention_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="American-led intervention in the Syrian Civil War">American-led intervention in Syria</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saudi-led_intervention_in_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi-led intervention in Yemen</a>. The active and effective military role, despite its small active personnel, has led the UAE military to be nicknamed as "Little Sparta" by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a> Generals and former US defense secretary <a href="/wiki/James_Mattis" class="mw-redirect" title="James Mattis">James Mattis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE intervened in the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Libyan Civil War (2014–present)">Libyan Civil War</a> in support of General <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Haftar" title="Khalifa Haftar">Khalifa Haftar</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Libyan_National_Army" title="Libyan National Army">Libyan National Army</a> in its conflict with the internationally recognised <a href="/wiki/Government_of_National_Accord" title="Government of National Accord">Government of National Accord</a> (GNA).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Examples of the military assets deployed include the enforcement of the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Odyssey_Dawn" title="Operation Odyssey Dawn">no-fly-zone over Libya</a> by sending six <a href="/wiki/UAEAF" class="mw-redirect" title="UAEAF">UAEAF</a> <a href="/wiki/F-16" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16">F-16</a> and six <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_2000" title="Dassault Mirage 2000">Mirage 2000</a> <a href="/wiki/Multirole_combat_aircraft" title="Multirole combat aircraft">multi-role fighter aircraft</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> ground troop deployment in Afghanistan,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> 30 UAEAF F-16s and ground troops deployment in Southern Yemen,<sup id="cite_ref-repel_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-repel-159">[159]</a></sup> and helping the US launch its first airstrikes against <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIL</a> targets in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE has begun production of a greater amount of military equipment, in a bid to reduce foreign dependence and help with national industrialisation. Example of national military development include the Abu Dhabi Shipbuilding company (ADSB), which produces a range of ships and is a prime contractor in the <a href="/wiki/Baynunah-class_corvette" title="Baynunah-class corvette">Baynunah Programme</a>, a programme to design, develop and produce corvettes customised for operation in the shallow waters of the Persian Gulf. The UAE is also producing weapons and ammunition through <a href="/wiki/Caracal_International" title="Caracal International">Caracal International</a>, military transport vehicles through <a href="/wiki/Nimr" title="Nimr">Nimr LLC</a> and unmanned aerial vehicles collectively through <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Defence_Industries_Company" title="Emirates Defence Industries Company">Emirates Defence Industries Company</a>. The UAE operates the <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon</a> F-16E Block 60 unique variant unofficially called "<a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon_variants#F-16E/F_Block_60" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon variants">Desert Falcon</a>", developed by General Dynamics with collaboration of the UAE and specifically for the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_Air_Force" title="United Arab Emirates Air Force">United Arab Emirates Air Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fg1_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg1-161">[161]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_Army" title="United Arab Emirates Army">United Arab Emirates Army</a> operates a customized <a href="/wiki/Leclerc_tank" title="Leclerc tank">Leclerc tank</a> and is the only other operator of the tank aside from the French Army.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The largest defence exhibition and conference in the Middle East, <a href="/wiki/International_Defence_Exhibition" title="International Defence Exhibition">International Defence Exhibition</a>, takes place biennially in Abu Dhabi. </p>
      <p>The UAE introduced a <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_National_Service_in_United_Arab_Emirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandatory National Service in United Arab Emirates">mandatory military service</a> for adult males, since 2014, for 16 months to expand its reserve force.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> The highest loss of life in the history of UAE military occurred on Friday 4 September 2015, in which 52 soldiers were killed in <a href="/wiki/Ma%27rib" class="mw-redirect" title="Ma'rib">Marib</a> area of central Yemen by a <a href="/wiki/OTR-21_Tochka" title="OTR-21 Tochka">Tochka</a> missile which targeted a weapons cache and caused a large explosion.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-164">[164]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions"><span class="anchor" id="Political_divisions"></span>Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Politics of the United Arab Emirates">Politics of the United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="List of cities in the United Arab Emirates">List of cities in the United Arab Emirates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Emirates of the United Arab Emirates">Emirates of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UAE_en-map.png" class="image" title="Location of the Emirates"><img alt="Location of the Emirates" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/UAE_en-map.png/590px-UAE_en-map.png" decoding="async" width="590" height="469" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/UAE_en-map.png/885px-UAE_en-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/UAE_en-map.png/1180px-UAE_en-map.png 2x" data-file-width="1414" data-file-height="1123"></a>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Arab Emirates comprises seven emirates. <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> is the most populous emirate with 35.6% of the UAE population. The <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_(emirate)" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Dhabi (emirate)">Emirate of Abu Dhabi</a> has 31.2%, meaning that over two-thirds of the UAE population lives in either Abu Dhabi or Dubai. </p>
      <p>Abu Dhabi has an area of 67,340 square kilometres (26,000 square miles), which is 86.7% of the country's total area, excluding the islands. It has a coastline extending for more than 400&nbsp;km (250&nbsp;mi) and is divided for administrative purposes into three major regions. The Emirate of Dubai extends along the Persian Gulf coast of the UAE for approximately 72&nbsp;km (45&nbsp;mi). Dubai has an area of 3,885 square kilometres (1,500 square miles), which is equivalent to 5% of the country's total area, excluding the islands. The Emirate of Sharjah extends along approximately 16&nbsp;km (10&nbsp;mi) of the UAE's Persian Gulf coastline and for more than 80&nbsp;km (50&nbsp;mi) into the interior. The northern emirates which include Fujairah, Ajman, Ras al-Khaimah, and <a href="/wiki/Umm_al-Quwain" class="mw-redirect" title="Umm al-Quwain">Umm al-Qaiwain</a> all have a total area of 3,881 square kilometres (1,498 square miles). There are two areas under joint control. One is jointly controlled by Oman and Ajman, the other by Fujairah and Sharjah. </p>
      <p>There is an Omani <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a> surrounded by UAE territory, known as <a href="/wiki/Madha" title="Madha">Wadi Madha</a>. It is located halfway between the <a href="/wiki/Musandam_Governorate" title="Musandam Governorate">Musandam</a> peninsula and the rest of Oman in the Emirate of <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>. It covers approximately 75 square kilometres (29 square miles) and the boundary was settled in 1969. The north-east corner of Madha is closest to the Khor Fakkan-Fujairah road, barely 10 metres (33 feet) away. Within the Omani exclave of Madha, is a UAE exclave called <a href="/wiki/Nahwa" title="Nahwa">Nahwa</a>, also belonging to the Emirate of Sharjah. It is about eight kilometres (5.0 miles) on a dirt track west of the town of New Madha. It consists of about forty houses with its own clinic and telephone exchange. </p>
