      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Legal_system_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Legal system of the United Arab Emirates">Legal system of the United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Crime in the United Arab Emirates">Crime in the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Police_helicopter_at_sunset_(Unsplash).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Police_helicopter_at_sunset_%28Unsplash%29.jpg/220px-Police_helicopter_at_sunset_%28Unsplash%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Police_helicopter_at_sunset_%28Unsplash%29.jpg/330px-Police_helicopter_at_sunset_%28Unsplash%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Police_helicopter_at_sunset_%28Unsplash%29.jpg/440px-Police_helicopter_at_sunset_%28Unsplash%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3410" data-file-height="2134"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Police_helicopter_at_sunset_(Unsplash).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Police">Dubai Police</a> helicopter flying at sunset.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE has a federal court system. There are three main branches within the court structure: civil, criminal and <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a>. The UAE's judicial system is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil law system">civil law system</a> and Sharia law. The court system consists of civil courts and Sharia courts. UAE's criminal and civil courts apply elements of Sharia law, codified into its criminal code and family law. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporal_and_capital_punishment">Corporal and capital punishment</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dubai_Police_at_work_(12385410394).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dubai_Police_at_work_%2812385410394%29.jpg/220px-Dubai_Police_at_work_%2812385410394%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dubai_Police_at_work_%2812385410394%29.jpg/330px-Dubai_Police_at_work_%2812385410394%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dubai_Police_at_work_%2812385410394%29.jpg/440px-Dubai_Police_at_work_%2812385410394%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3159" data-file-height="1973"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dubai_Police_at_work_(12385410394).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Police">Dubai Police</a> super-car motorcade at <a href="/wiki/Jumeirah_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Jumeirah Road">Jumeirah Road</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_(Official_Press)_(18015081283).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_%28Official_Press%29_%2818015081283%29.jpg/220px-Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_%28Official_Press%29_%2818015081283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_%28Official_Press%29_%2818015081283%29.jpg/330px-Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_%28Official_Press%29_%2818015081283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_%28Official_Press%29_%2818015081283%29.jpg/440px-Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_%28Official_Press%29_%2818015081283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="3337"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_Police_-_Lykan_Hypersport_(Official_Press)_(18015081283).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_Police" title="Abu Dhabi Police">Abu Dhabi Police</a> patrol car on duty at the <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Palace" title="Emirates Palace">Emirates Palace</a> hotel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Flogging" class="mw-redirect" title="Flogging">Flogging</a> is a punishment for criminal offences such as <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">adultery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Premarital_sex" title="Premarital sex">premarital sex</a> and alcohol consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-usdep_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usdep-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-flog_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flog-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> According to Sharia court rulings, flogging ranges from 80 to 200 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-usdep_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usdep-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Verbal abuse pertaining to a person's honour is illegal and punishable by 80 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Between 2007 and 2014, many people in the UAE were sentenced to 100 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-khaleejtimes.com_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khaleejtimes.com-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-emirates1_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emirates1-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="Too many citations for sources to be verifiable (May 2021)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup> More recently in 2015, two men were sentenced to 80 lashes for hitting and insulting a woman.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> In 2014, an <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> in Abu Dhabi was sentenced to 10 years in prison and 80 lashes after alcohol consumption and raping a toddler.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> As of November 2020, Alcohol consumption for Muslims and non Muslims is legal. In the past, many Muslims have been sentenced to 80 or 40 lashes for alcohol consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="Too many citations for sources to be verifiable (May 2021)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup> Illicit sex is sometimes penalized by 60 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> 80 lashes is the standard number for anyone sentenced to flogging in several emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Sharia courts have penalized domestic workers with floggings.<sup id="cite_ref-drm_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drm-198">[198]</a></sup> In October 2013, a Filipino housemaid was sentenced to 100 lashes for illegitimate pregnancy.<sup id="cite_ref-emirates1_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emirates1-178">[178]</a></sup> Drunk-driving is strictly illegal and punishable by 80 lashes; many expatriates have been sentenced to 80 lashes for drunk-driving.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="Too many citations for sources to be verifiable (May 2021)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup> Under UAE law, premarital sex is punishable by 100 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">Stoning</a> is a legal punishment in the UAE. In May 2014, an Asian housemaid was sentenced to death by stoning in Abu Dhabi.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Other expatriates have been sentenced to death by stoning for committing adultery.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> Between 2009 and 2013, several people were sentenced to death by stoning.<sup id="cite_ref-khaleejtimes.com_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khaleejtimes.com-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Abortion is illegal and punishable by a maximum penalty of 100 lashes and up to five years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> In recent years, several people have retracted their guilty plea in illicit sex cases after being sentenced to stoning or 100 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> The punishment for committing adultery is 100 lashes for unmarried people and stoning to death for married people.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">Amputation</a> is a legal punishment in the UAE due to the Sharia courts.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion" title="Crucifixion">Crucifixion</a> is a legal punishment in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Article 1 of the Federal Penal Code states that "provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Law">Islamic Law</a> shall apply to the crimes of doctrinal punishment, punitive punishment and blood money."<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> The Federal Penal Code repealed only those provisions within the penal codes of individual emirates which are contradictory to the Federal Penal Code. Hence, both are enforceable simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sharia_courts_and_family_law">Sharia courts and family law</span></h3> 
      <p>Sharia courts have exclusive jurisdiction over family law cases and also have jurisdiction over several criminal cases including adultery, premarital sex, robbery, alcohol consumption and related crimes. The Sharia-based <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">personal status law</a> regulates matters such as marriage, divorce and child custody. The Islamic personal status law is applied to Muslims and sometimes non-Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-lia_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lia-227">[227]</a></sup> Non-Muslim expatriates can be liable to Sharia rulings on marriage, divorce and child custody.<sup id="cite_ref-lia_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lia-227">[227]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Emirati women must receive permission from a male guardian to marry and remarry.<sup id="cite_ref-maleguardian_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maleguardian-228">[228]</a></sup> This requirement is derived from the UAE's interpretation of Sharia, and has been federal law since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-maleguardian_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maleguardian-228">[228]</a></sup> In all emirates, it is illegal for Muslim women to marry non-Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-229">[229]</a></sup> In the UAE, a marriage union between a Muslim woman and non-Muslim man is punishable by law, since it is considered a form of "<a href="/wiki/Fornication" title="Fornication">fornication</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-229">[229]</a></sup> The UAE Marriage Fund reported in 2012 that a majority of women over 30 were unmarried; this had tripled from 1995, when only one-fifth of women over 30 were unmarried.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kissing in public is illegal and can result in <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deportation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-231">[231]</a></sup> Expats in Dubai have been deported for kissing in public.<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gulfnews_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gulfnews-233">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-234">[234]</a></sup> In Abu Dhabi, people have been sentenced to 80 lashes for kissing in public.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> A new federal law in the UAE prohibits swearing in <a href="/wiki/Whatsapp" class="mw-redirect" title="Whatsapp">Whatsapp</a> and penalizes swearing by a 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Emirati_dirham" class="mw-redirect" title="Emirati dirham">AED</a> fine and imprisonment;<sup id="cite_ref-inde_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inde-236">[236]</a></sup> expatriates are penalized by deportation.<sup id="cite_ref-inde_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inde-236">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> In July 2015, an Australian expatriate was deported for swearing on Facebook.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="LGBT rights in the United Arab Emirates">Homosexuality</a> is illegal and is a <a href="/wiki/Capital_offence" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital offence">capital offence</a> in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arc.com_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc.com-245">[245]</a></sup> In 2013, an Emirati man was on trial for being accused of a "gay handshake".<sup id="cite_ref-arc.com_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc.com-245">[245]</a></sup> Article 80 of the Abu Dhabi Penal Code makes sodomy punishable with imprisonment of up to 14 years, while article 177 of the Penal Code of Dubai imposes imprisonment of up to 10 years on consensual sodomy.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2020, UAE announced that it decriminalised alcohol, lifted ban on unmarried couples living together and ended clement punishment on <a href="/wiki/Honor_killing" title="Honor killing">honor killing</a>. Foreigners living in the Emirates were allowed to follow their native country's laws on divorce and inheritance.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blasphemy_law">Blasphemy law</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Apostasy" title="Apostasy">Apostasy</a> is a crime <a href="/wiki/Punishable_by_death" class="mw-redirect" title="Punishable by death">punishable by death</a> in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy" title="Blasphemy">Blasphemy</a> is illegal; expatriates involved in insulting Islam are liable for deportation.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> UAE incorporates <a href="/wiki/Hudud" title="Hudud">hudud</a> crimes of Sharia (i.e., crimes against God) into its Penal Code – apostasy being one of them.<sup id="cite_ref-shar_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shar-251">[251]</a></sup> Article 1 and Article 66 of UAE's <a href="/wiki/Penal_Code" class="mw-redirect" title="Penal Code">Penal Code</a> requires hudud crimes to be punished with the death penalty;<sup id="cite_ref-shar_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shar-251">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> therefore, apostasy is punishable by death in the UAE. </p>
      <p>In several cases, the courts of the UAE have jailed women who have reported rape.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-254">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tdb_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdb-255">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nydaily_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydaily-256">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-latimes_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-257">[257]</a></sup> For example, a British woman, after she reported being gang raped by three men, was charged with the crime of "alcohol consumption".<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nydaily_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydaily-256">[256]</a></sup> Another British woman was charged with "public intoxication and extramarital sex" after she reported being raped,<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_254-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-254">[254]</a></sup> while an Australian woman was similarly sentenced to jail after she reported gang rape in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_254-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-254">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-71">[71]</a></sup> In another recent case, an 18-year Emirati girl withdrew her complaint of gang rape by six men when the prosecution threatened her with a long jail term and flogging.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-258">[258]</a></sup> The woman still had to serve one year in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-arabianbusiness_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabianbusiness-259">[259]</a></sup> In July 2013, a <a href="/wiki/Prosecution_of_Marte_Dalelv" title="Prosecution of Marte Dalelv">Norwegian woman, Marte Dalelv</a>, reported rape to the police and received a prison sentence for "illicit sex and alcohol consumption".<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_254-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-254">[254]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the month of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, it is illegal to publicly eat, drink, or smoke between sunrise and sunset.<sup id="cite_ref-ramadan_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramadan-260">[260]</a></sup> Exceptions are made for pregnant women and children. The law applies to both Muslims and non-Muslims,<sup id="cite_ref-ramadan_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramadan-260">[260]</a></sup> and failure to comply may result in arrest,<sup id="cite_ref-Riazat_Butt_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riazat_Butt-261">[261]</a></sup> however, this law is disappearing year by year due to the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2020" title="Expo 2020">Expo 2020</a> in Dubai. Dancing in public is illegal in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Human rights in the United Arab Emirates">Human rights in the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Flogging" class="mw-redirect" title="Flogging">Flogging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">stoning</a> are legal punishments in the UAE. The requirement is derived from <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a>, and has been federal law since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-265">[265]</a></sup> Some domestic workers in the UAE are victims of the country's interpretations of Sharia judicial punishments such as flogging and stoning.<sup id="cite_ref-drm_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drm-198">[198]</a></sup> The annual <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> report on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> has listed the United Arab Emirates as "Not Free" every year since 1999, the first year for which records are available on their website.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Arab_Emirates_Reports_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Arab_Emirates_Reports-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_!.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg/220px-Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg/330px-Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg/440px-Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2474" data-file-height="2458"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_!.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Protest against the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>, March 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE has escaped the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>; however, more than 100 Emirati activists were jailed and <a href="/wiki/Tortured" class="mw-redirect" title="Tortured">tortured</a> because they sought reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-267">[267]</a></sup> Since 2011, the UAE government has increasingly carried out <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced disappearances">forced disappearances</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aohr_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hrw_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-270">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> Many foreign nationals and Emirati citizens have been arrested and abducted by the state. The UAE government denies these people are being held (to conceal their whereabouts), placing these people outside the protection of the law.<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-267">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aohr_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> According to Human Rights Watch, the reports of forced disappearance and torture in the UAE are of grave concern.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-270">[270]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Arab_Organization_for_Human_Rights" title="Arab Organization for Human Rights">Arab Organization for Human Rights</a> has obtained testimonies from many defendants, for its report on "Forced Disappearance and Torture in the UAE", who reported that they had been kidnapped, tortured and abused in detention centres.<sup id="cite_ref-aohr_269-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> The report included 16 different methods of torture including severe beatings, threats with <a href="/wiki/Electrocution" title="Electrocution">electrocution</a> and denying access to medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-aohr_269-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, 94 Emirati activists were held in secret detention centres and put on trial for allegedly attempting to overthrow the government.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> Human rights organizations have spoken out against the secrecy of the trial. An Emirati, whose father is among the defendants, was arrested for tweeting about the trial. In April 2013, he was sentenced to 10 months in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> The latest forced disappearance involves <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_the_Al-Suwaidi_sisters" title="Disappearance of the Al-Suwaidi sisters">three sisters from Abu Dhabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-277">[277]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Repressive measures were also used against non-Emiratis in order to justify the UAE government's claim that there is an "international plot" in which UAE citizens and foreigners were working together to destabilize the country.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> Foreign nationals were also subjected to a campaign of deportations.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> There are many documented cases of Egyptians and other foreign nationals who had spent years working in the UAE and were then given only a few days to leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Foreign nationals subjected to forced disappearance include two <a href="/wiki/Libyans" class="mw-redirect" title="Libyans">Libyans</a><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> and two Qataris.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qta_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qta-279">[279]</a></sup> Amnesty reported that the Qatari men have been abducted by the UAE government and the UAE government has withheld information about the men's fate from their families.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qta_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qta-279">[279]</a></sup> Amongst the foreign nationals detained, imprisoned and expelled is <a href="/wiki/Iyad_El-Baghdadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Iyad El-Baghdadi">Iyad El-Baghdadi</a>, a popular blogger and Twitter personality.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> He was arrested by UAE authorities, detained, imprisoned and then expelled from the country.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> Despite his lifetime residence in the UAE, as a Palestinian citizen, El-Baghdadi had no recourse to contest this order.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> He could not be deported back to the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a>, therefore he was deported to Malaysia.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_274-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-274">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, the UAE government attempted to cover up information on the rape of a French teenage boy by three Emirati locals, one of whose HIV-positive status was hidden by Emirati authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-nov1rapecase_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nov1rapecase-280">[280]</a></sup> Diplomatic pressure led to the arrest and conviction of the Emirati rapists.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2009, a video tape of <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> smuggled out of the UAE showed Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Issa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Issa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Issa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> torturing a man (Mohammed Shah Poor) with whips, electric cattle prods, wooden planks with protruding nails and running him over repeatedly with a car.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> In December 2009, Issa appeared in court and proclaimed his innocence.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakr1_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakr1-283">[283]</a></sup> The trial ended on 10 January 2010, when Issa was cleared of the torture of Mohammed Shah Poor.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakr2_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakr2-284">[284]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> criticised the trial and called on the government to establish an independent body to investigate allegations of abuse by UAE security personnel and other persons of authority.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/US_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> has expressed concern over the verdict and said all members of Emirati society "must stand equal before the law" and called for a careful review of the decision to ensure that the demands of justice are fully met in this case.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, many <a href="/wiki/Shia_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Muslim">Shia Muslim</a> expatriates have been deported from the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> Lebanese Shia families in particular have been deported for their alleged sympathy for <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> According to some organizations, more than 4,000 Shia expatriates have been deported from the UAE in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The issue of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> among female <a href="/wiki/Domestic_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic workers">domestic workers</a> is another area of concern, particularly given that domestic servants are not covered by the UAE labour law of 1980 or the draft labour law of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> Worker protests have been suppressed and protesters imprisoned without due process.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> In its 2013 Annual Report, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> drew attention to the United Arab Emirates' poor record on a number of human rights issues. They highlighted the government's restrictive approach to freedom of speech and assembly, their use of <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest_and_detention" title="Arbitrary arrest and detention">arbitrary arrest</a> and torture, and UAE's use of the death penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, Dubai police subjected three British citizens to <a href="/wiki/Battery_(crime)" title="Battery (crime)">beatings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_shocks" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric shocks">electric shocks</a> after arresting them on drugs charges.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> The British Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, expressed "concern" over the case and raised it with the UAE President, Sheikh Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan, during his 2013 state visit to the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> The three men were pardoned and released in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, police arrested a US citizen and some UAE citizens, in connection with a <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> parody video which allegedly portrayed Dubai and its residents in a bad light. The video was shot in areas of <a href="/wiki/Satwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Satwa">Satwa</a>, Dubai, and featured gangs learning how to fight using simple weapons, including shoes, the aghal, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> In 2015, nationals from different countries were put in jail for offences. An Australian woman was accused of 'writing bad words on social media' after she had posted a picture of a vehicle parked illegally. She was later deported from the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The State Security Apparatus in the UAE has been accused of a series of atrocities and human rights abuses including enforced disappearance, arbitrary arrests and torture,<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Freedom of association is also severely curtailed. All associations and NGOs have to register through the Ministry of Social Affairs and are therefore under de facto State control. About twenty non-political groups operate on the territory without registration. All associations have to be submitted to censorship guidelines and all publications have first to be approved by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In a report released on 12 July 2018, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> urged for probe of torture claims on UAE-run prisons in <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 10 September 2018, Yemeni detainees in a UAE-run prison underwent a hunger strike to protest their detention. Despite orders by the prosecutors to release some of the detained prisoners, the detainees are still being held.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 30 September 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Center_for_Human_Rights" title="Gulf Center for Human Rights">Gulf Centre for Human Rights</a> (GCHR) reported that <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Mansoor" title="Ahmed Mansoor">Ahmed Mansoor</a> was beaten up by the <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> Al-Sadr Prison authorities for holding a hunger strike against his imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2020, a British court ruled that on the balance of probabilities, the prime minister of the UAE and ruler of Dubai, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Rashid_Al_Maktoum" title="Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum">Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum</a>, had abducted two of his daughters and had threatened his former wife, <a href="/wiki/Haya_bint_Hussein" class="mw-redirect" title="Haya bint Hussein">Princess Haya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC5320_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC5320-311">[311]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2020, US-based Gulf rights group ADHRB (Americans for Democracy and Human Rights in Bahrain) criticized the <a href="/wiki/UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="UAE">UAE</a> for practicing the culture of "impunity". Emirati authorities are accused of using torture methods against those they perceive as a threat; this "threat" most commonly refers to human rights defenders, political opposition, religious figures, and journalists, said ADHRB in its report.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2020, a report by <i><a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a></i> stated that it uncovered evidence confirming that the UAE-operated <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drones</a> killed 26 cadets in January 2020, at a military academy in <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>. An investigation by BBC Africa Eye and BBC Arabic Documentaries revealed that a <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/HJ-10" title="HJ-10">Blue Arrow 7</a> missile was used in the strike. Besides, the sophisticated weapon was fired using the UAE-operated <a href="/wiki/Wing_Loong_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Wing Loong II">Wing Loong II</a> drone, which were solely being operated from the Emirates’ Al-Khadim air base in <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, during that time.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migrant_workers">Migrant workers</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Migrant workers in the United Arab Emirates">Migrant workers in the United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_Gulf_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers in the Gulf region">Migrant workers in the Gulf region</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg/220px-Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg/330px-Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg/440px-Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1229" data-file-height="848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Two south Asian <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue-collar workers">blue-collar workers</a> posing for a picture with <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> on the background.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Migrant workers in the UAE are not allowed to join trade unions or go on strike. Those who strike may risk prison and deportation,<sup id="cite_ref-mig_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mig-315">[315]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> as seen in 2014 when dozens of workers were deported for striking.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="International Trade Union Confederation">International Trade Union Confederation</a> has called on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> to investigate evidence that thousands of migrant workers in the UAE are treated as slave labour.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A report In January 2020 highlighted that the employers in the United Arab Emirates have been exploiting the <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> labor and hiring them on <a href="/wiki/Travel_visa" title="Travel visa">tourist visas</a>, which is easier and cheaper than <a href="/wiki/Work_permit" title="Work permit">work permits</a>. These <a href="/wiki/Migrant_worker" title="Migrant worker">migrant workers</a> are left open to <a href="/wiki/Labor_rights" title="Labor rights">labor abuse</a>, where they also fear reporting exploitation due to their illegal status. Besides, the issue remains unknown as the visit visa data is not maintained in both the UAE and Indian <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> and employment records.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In a 22 July 2020 news piece, Reuters reported <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> groups as saying conditions had deteriorated because of the <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">coronavirus pandemic</a>. Many migrant workers racked up debt and depended on the help of charities. The report cited salary delays and layoffs as a major risk, in addition to overcrowded living conditions, lack of support and problems linked with healthcare and sick pay. Reuters reported at least 200,000 workers, mostly from India but also from Pakistan, Bangladesh, the Philippines and Nepal, had been repatriated, according to their diplomatic missions.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 2 May 2020, the Consul General of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, Vipul, confirmed that more than 150,000 Indians in the United Arab Emirates registered to be repatriated through the e-registration option provided by Indian consulates in the UAE. According to the figures, 25% applicants lost their jobs and nearly 15% were stranded in the country due to lockdown. Besides, 50% of the total applicants were from the state of <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, India.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 9 October 2020, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i> reported that many migrant workers were left abandoned, as they lost their jobs amidst the tightening economy due to <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>. With no jobs and expired visas, many hived in parks under the city's glistening skyscrapers, appealing for repatriation flights home. White collar job workers were also threatened by the pandemic in the Emirates, as many <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> expats returned home since the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus" title="Coronavirus">coronavirus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dress_code">Dress code</span></h3> 
      <p>The UAE has a modest dress code, which is part of Dubai's criminal law.<sup id="cite_ref-Criminal_Law_of_Dubai_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Criminal_Law_of_Dubai-323">[323]</a></sup> Most malls in the UAE have a dress code displayed at entrances.<sup id="cite_ref-code_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-code-324">[324]</a></sup> At Dubai's malls, women are encouraged to cover their shoulders and knees.<sup id="cite_ref-code_324-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-code-324">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modest_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modest-325">[325]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dubai_Mall_dress_code_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dubai_Mall_dress_code-326">[326]</a></sup> Despite this, people are allowed to wear swimwear at pools and beaches. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2> 
      <p>The UAE's <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of the United Arab Emirates">media</a> is annually classified as "not free" in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_Press_(report)" title="Freedom of the Press (report)">Freedom of the Press</a> report by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> The UAE ranks poorly in the annual <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_without_Borders" class="mw-redirect" title="Reporters without Borders">Reporters without Borders</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Media_City" title="Dubai Media City">Dubai Media City</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Twofour54&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Twofour54 (page does not exist)">twofour54</a> are the UAE's main media zones. The UAE is home to some pan-Arab broadcasters, including the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Broadcasting_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle East Broadcasting Centre">Middle East Broadcasting Centre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orbit_Showtime_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Orbit Showtime Network">Orbit Showtime Network</a>. In 2007, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Rashid_Al_Maktoum" title="Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum">Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum</a> decreed that journalists can no longer be prosecuted or imprisoned for reasons relating to their work.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> At the same time, the UAE has made it illegal to disseminate online material that can threaten "public order",<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> and hands down prison terms for those who "deride or damage" the reputation of the state and "display contempt" for religion.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Economy of the United Arab Emirates">Economy of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Khalifa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Burj_Khalifa.jpg/170px-Burj_Khalifa.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Burj_Khalifa.jpg/255px-Burj_Khalifa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Burj_Khalifa.jpg/340px-Burj_Khalifa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3279" data-file-height="5740"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Khalifa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in the world">tallest human-made structure in the world</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE has developed from a juxtaposition of Bedouin tribes to one of the world's most wealthy states in only about 50 years. Economic growth has been impressive and steady throughout the history of this young confederation of emirates with brief periods of recessions only, e.g. in the global financial and economic crisis years 2008–09, and a couple of more mixed years starting in 2015 and persisting until 2019. Between 2000 and 2018, average real Gross Domestic Product (GDP) growth was at close to 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> It is the second largest economy in the GCC (after Saudi Arabia),<sup id="cite_ref-Economy2013_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy2013-332">[332]</a></sup> with a nominal gross domestic product (GDP) of US$414.2 billion, and a real GDP of 392.8 billion constant 2010 USD in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> Since its independence in 1971, the UAE's economy has grown by nearly 231 times to 1.45 trillion AED in 2013. The non-oil trade has grown to 1.2 trillion AED, a growth by around 28 times from 1981 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy2013_332-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy2013-332">[332]</a></sup> Backed by the world's seventh-largest oil deposits, and thanks to considerate investments combined with decided economic liberalism and firm Government control, the UAE has seen their real GDP more than triple in the last four decades. Nowadays the UAE is one of the world's richest countries, with GDP per capita almost 80% higher than OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As impressive as economic growth has been in the UAE, the total population has increased from just around 550,000 in 1975 to close to 10 million in 2018. This growth is mainly due to the influx of foreign workers into the country, making the national population a minority. The UAE features a unique labour market system, in which residence in the UAE is conditional on stringent visa rules. This system is a major advantage in terms of macroeconomic stability, as labour supply adjusts quickly to demand throughout economic business cycles. This allows the Government to keep unemployment in the country on a very low level of less than 3%, and it also gives the Government more leeway in terms of macroeconomic policies – where other governments often need to make trade-offs between fighting unemployment and fighting inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 2014 and 2018, the accommodation and food, education, information and communication, arts and recreation, and real estate sectors overperformed in terms of growth, whereas the construction, logistics, professional services, public, and oil and gas sectors underperformed.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_finance">Business and finance</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg/220px-Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg/330px-Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg/440px-Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5726" data-file-height="3143"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Abu Dhabi skyline
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UAE offers businesses a strong enabling environment: stable political and macroeconomic conditions, a future-oriented Government, good general infrastructure and ICT infrastructure. Moreover, the country has made continuous and convincing improvements to its regulatory environment<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> and is ranked as the 26th best nation in the world for doing business by the <a href="/wiki/Doing_Business_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Doing Business Report">Doing Business 2017 Report</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Doing_Business_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_Business-333">[333]</a></sup> The UAE are in the top ranks of several other global indices, such as the World Economic Forum's (WEF) Global Competitiveness Index (GCI), the World Happiness Report (WHR) and the Global Innovation Index (GII). The Economist Intelligence Unit (EIU), for example, assigns the UAE rank two regionally in terms of business environment and 22 worldwide. From the 2018 Arab Youth Survey the UAE emerges as the top Arab country in areas such as living, safety and security, economic opportunities, and starting a business, and as an example for other states to emulate.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The weaker points remain the level of education across the UAE population, limitations in the financial and labour markets, barriers to trade and some regulations that hinder business dynamism. The major challenge for the country, though, remains translating investments and strong enabling conditions into knowledge, innovation and creative outputs.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>UAE law does not allow trade unions to exist.<sup id="cite_ref-ituc_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ituc-334">[334]</a></sup> The right to <a href="/wiki/Collective_bargaining" title="Collective bargaining">collective bargaining</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to strike">right to strike</a> are not recognised, and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Labour" title="Ministry of Labour">Ministry of Labour</a> has the power to force workers to go back to work. Migrant workers who participate in a strike can have their work permits cancelled and be deported.<sup id="cite_ref-ituc_334-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ituc-334">[334]</a></sup> Consequently, there are very few anti-discrimination laws in relation to labour issues, with Emiratis – and other <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">GCC</a> Arabs – getting preference in public sector jobs despite lesser credentials than competitors and lower motivation. In fact, just over eighty percent of Emirati workers hold government posts, with many of the rest taking part in state-owned enterprises such as <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Properties" title="Dubai Properties">Dubai Properties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE's monetary policy stresses stability and predictability, as the Central Bank of the UAE (CBUAE) keeps a peg to the US Dollar (USD) and moves interest rates close to the Federal Funds Rate. This policy makes sense in the current situation of global and regional economic and geopolitical uncertainty. Also considering the fact that exports have become the main driver of the UAE's economic growth (the contribution of international trade to GDP grew from 31% in 2017 to 33.5% in 2018, outpacing overall GDP growth for the period), and the fact that the AED is currently undervalued, a departure from this policy – and particularly the peg – would negatively affect this important part of the UAE economy in the short term. In the mid- to long term, however, the peg will become less important, as the UAE transitions to a knowledge-based economy – and becomes yet more independent from the oil and gas sector (oil is currently still being traded not in AED, but in USD). On the contrary, it will become more and more important for the Government to have monetary policy at its free disposal to target inflation, shun too heavy reliance on taxes, and avoid situations where decisions on exchange rates and interest rates contradict fiscal policy measures – as has been the case in recent years, where monetary policy has limited fiscal policy effects on economic expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch Ratings</a>, the decline in property sector follows risks of progressively worsening the quality of assets in possession with UAE banks, leading the economy to rougher times ahead. Even though as compared to retail and property, UAE banks fared well. The higher US interest rates followed since 2016 – which the UAE currency complies to – have boosted profitability. However, the likelihood of plunging interest rates and increasing provisioning costs on bad loans, point to difficult times ahead for the <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2015, economic growth has been more mixed due to a number of factors impacting both demand and supply. In 2017 and 2018 growth has been positive but on a low level of 0.8 and 1.4%, respectively. To support the economy the Government is currently following an expansionary fiscal policy. However, the effects of this policy are partially offset by monetary policy, which has been contractionary. If not for the fiscal stimulus in 2018, the UAE economy would probably have contracted in that year. One of the factors responsible for slower growth has been a credit crunch, which is due to, among other factors, higher interest rates. Government debt has remained on a low level, despite high deficits in a few recent years. Risks related to government debt remain low. Inflation has been picking up in 2017 and 18. Contributing factors were the introduction of a value added tax (VAT) of 5% in 2018 as well as higher commodity prices. Despite the Government's expansionary fiscal policy and a growing economy in 2018 and at the beginning of 2019, prices have been dropping in late 2018 and 2019 owing to oversupply in some sectors of importance to consumer prices.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2020, a <a href="/wiki/UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="UAE">UAE</a>-based firm, Essentra FZE agreed to pay a fine of $665,112 to the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Justice">US Department of Justice</a>. The firm defrauded the <a href="/wiki/US_sanctions" class="mw-redirect" title="US sanctions">US sanctions</a> on <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> by devising a criminal scheme to use a deceitful network of front companies and financial entities to manipulate <a href="/wiki/US" class="mw-redirect" title="US">US</a> banks into processing prohibited US dollar transactions for benefiting North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE has an attractive tax system for companies and wealthy individuals, making it a preferred destination for companies seeking to <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">tax avoidance</a>. The NGO <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">Tax Justice Network</a> places them in 2021 in the group of the ten largest <a href="/wiki/Tax_havens" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax havens">tax havens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_gas">Oil and gas</span></h3> 
      <p>The UAE leadership has driven forward economic diversification efforts already before the oil price crash in the 1980s, and the UAE is nowadays the most diversified economy in the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">Middle East and North Africa</a> (MENA) region. Although the oil and gas sector does still play an important role in the UAE economy, these efforts have paid off in terms of great resilience during periods of oil price fluctuations and economic turbulence. In 2018, the oil and gas sector contributed 26% to overall GDP. The introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">VAT</a> has provided the Government with an additional source of income – approximately 6% of the total revenue in 2018, or 27 billion <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_dirham" title="United Arab Emirates dirham">United Arab Emirates Dirham</a> (AED) – affording its fiscal policy more independence from oil- and gas-related revenue, which constitutes about 36% of the total Government revenue. While the Government may still adjust the exact arrangement of the VAT, it is not likely that any new taxes will be introduced in the foreseeable future. Additional taxes would destroy one of the UAE's main enticements for businesses to operate in the country and put a heavy burden on the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_331-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-331">[331]</a></sup> The UAE <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions_per_capita" title="List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita">emits a lot of carbon dioxide per person</a> compared to other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg/220px-Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="89" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg/330px-Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg/440px-Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4832" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Marina" title="Dubai Marina">Dubai Marina</a> Beach
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism acts as a growth sector for the entire UAE economy. <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> is the top tourism destination in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-tdb_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdb-255">[255]</a></sup> According to the annual MasterCard Global Destination Cities Index, Dubai is the fifth most popular tourism destination in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup> Dubai holds up to 66% share of the UAE's tourism economy, with <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> having 16% and <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a> 10%. Dubai welcomed 10 million tourists in 2013. </p>
      <p>The UAE has the most advanced and developed infrastructure in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> Since the 1980s, the UAE has been spending billions of dollars on infrastructure. These developments are particularly evident in the larger emirates of Abu Dhabi and Dubai. The northern emirates are rapidly following suit, providing major incentives for developers of residential and commercial property.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 6 January 2020, <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Mohammed_Bin_Rashid_Al_Maktoum" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Mohammed Bin Rashid Al Maktoum">Prime Minister Sheikh Mohammed Bin Rashid Al Maktoum</a> announced that the tourist visa to the United Arab Emirates, which was earlier valid for 30–90 days, was extended to five years.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Transport in the United Arab Emirates">Transport in the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span></h4> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Airbus_A380_(A6-EDS)_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg/190px-Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="139" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg/285px-Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg/380px-Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4653" data-file-height="3401"></a>
