       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai International Airport</a> became the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by international passenger traffic">busiest airport in the world by international passenger traffic</a> in 2014, overtaking <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajman" title="Ajman">Ajman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umm_Al_Quwain" title="Umm Al Quwain">Umm Al Quwain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Ras_Al_Khaimah" title="Emirate of Ras Al Khaimah">Ras Al Khaimah</a> are connected by the <a href="/wiki/E_11_road_(United_Arab_Emirates)" title="E 11 road (United Arab Emirates)">E11 highway</a>, which is the longest road in the UAE. In Dubai, in addition to the metro, <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Tram" title="Dubai Tram">Dubai Tram</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palm_Jumeirah_Monorail" title="Palm Jumeirah Monorail">Palm Jumeirah Monorail</a> also connect specific parts of the city. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png/220px-5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png/330px-5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png/440px-5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png 2x" data-file-width="2256" data-file-height="1650"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:5018_Dubai_Metro_in_Dubai_UAE.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Metro" title="Dubai Metro">Dubai Metro</a> train
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A 1,200&nbsp;km (750&nbsp;mi) <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Rail transport in the United Arab Emirates">country-wide railway</a> is under construction which will connect all the major cities and ports.<sup id="cite_ref-IRJMar12_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRJMar12-345">[345]</a></sup> The Dubai Metro is the first urban train network in the Arabian Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span></h4> 
      <p>The major ports of the United Arab Emirates are <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Port" title="Khalifa Port">Khalifa Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayed_Port" title="Zayed Port">Zayed Port</a>, Port <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Ali" title="Jebel Ali">Jebel Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Rashid" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Rashid">Port Rashid</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Port_Khalid&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Port Khalid (page does not exist)">Port Khalid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Saeed" title="Port Saeed">Port Saeed</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Port_Khor_Fakkan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Port Khor Fakkan (page does not exist)">Port Khor Fakkan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup> The Emirates are increasingly developing their logistics and ports in order to participate in trade between Europe and China or Africa. For this purpose, ports are being rapidly expanded and investments being made in their technology. </p>
      <p>The Emirates are historically and currently part of the Maritime <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> that runs from the Chinese coast to the south via the southern tip of India to <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, from there through the Red Sea via the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> to the Mediterranean, there to the Upper Adriatic region and the northern Italian hub of <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> with its rail connections to <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, Eastern Europe and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3> 
      <p>The UAE is served by two <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunications</a> operators, <a href="/wiki/Etisalat" title="Etisalat">Etisalat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Integrated_Telecommunications_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company">Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company</a> ("du"). Etisalat operated a <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a> until du launched mobile services in February 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-etisalatmon_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etisalatmon-350">[350]</a></sup> Internet subscribers were expected to increase from 0.904 million in 2007 to 2.66 million in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> The regulator, the <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_Regulatory_Authority_(UAE)" title="Telecommunications Regulatory Authority (UAE)">Telecommunications Regulatory Authority</a>, mandates filtering websites for religious, political and sexual content.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">5G</a> wireless services were installed nationwide in 2019 through a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Culture of the United Arab Emirates">Culture of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Emirati_Dialect" title="Emirati Dialect">Emirati Dialect</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg/220px-Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg/330px-Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg/440px-Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="630"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Souq" class="mw-redirect" title="Souq">souk</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Deira,_Dubai" title="Deira, Dubai">Deira</a>, Dubai
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Emirati culture is based on <a href="/wiki/Arabian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabian culture">Arabian culture</a> and has been influenced by the cultures of <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persia</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, and <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-folk_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folk-354">[354]</a></sup> Arabian and <a href="/wiki/Persian_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian architecture">Persian inspired architecture</a> is part of the expression of the local Emirati identity.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-355">[355]</a></sup> Persian influence on Emirati culture is noticeably visible in traditional Emirati architecture and <a href="/wiki/Folk_arts" title="Folk arts">folk arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-folk_354-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folk-354">[354]</a></sup> For example, the distinctive wind tower which tops traditional Emirati buildings, the <i><a href="/wiki/Barjeel" class="mw-redirect" title="Barjeel">barjeel</a></i> has become an identifying mark of Emirati architecture and is attributed to Persian influence.<sup id="cite_ref-folk_354-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folk-354">[354]</a></sup> This influence is derived both from traders who fled the tax regime in Persia in the early 19th century and from Emirati ownership of ports on the Persian coast, for instance the Al Qassimi port of Lingeh.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Haribya_Band.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Haribya_Band.jpg/220px-Haribya_Band.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Haribya_Band.jpg/330px-Haribya_Band.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Haribya_Band.jpg/440px-Haribya_Band.jpg 2x" data-file-width="964" data-file-height="715"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Haribya_Band.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A band performs a razfah in an Emirati wedding. Razfah is a cultural dance derived from Arab tribes sword battles.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Arab Emirates has a diverse society.<sup id="cite_ref-migrationinformation_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migrationinformation-357">[357]</a></sup> Dubai's economy depends more on international trade and tourism, and is more open to visitors, while Abu Dhabi society is more domestic as the city's economy is focused on fossil fuel extraction.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[358]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Major holidays in the United Arab Emirates include <i><a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid al Fitr</a></i>, which marks the end of <i><a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/National_Day_(United_Arab_Emirates)" title="National Day (United Arab Emirates)">National Day</a> (2 December), which marks the formation of the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup> Emirati males prefer to wear a <a href="/wiki/Thawb" title="Thawb">kandura</a>, an ankle-length white tunic woven from wool or cotton, and Emirati women wear an <a href="/wiki/Abaya" title="Abaya">abaya</a>, a black over-garment that covers most parts of the body.<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ancient Emirati poetry was strongly influenced by the 8th-century Arab scholar Al Khalil bin Ahmed. The earliest known poet in the UAE is <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Majid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn Majid">Ibn Majid</a>, born between 1432 and 1437 in Ras Al-Khaimah. The most famous Emirati writers were Mubarak Al Oqaili (1880–1954), Salem bin Ali al Owais (1887–1959) and Ahmed bin Sulayem (1905–1976). Three other poets from Sharjah, known as the Hirah group, are observed to have been heavily influenced by the Apollo and <a href="/wiki/Romantic_poetry" title="Romantic poetry">Romantic poets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-poetry_361-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poetry-361">[361]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_International_Book_Fair" title="Sharjah International Book Fair">Sharjah International Book Fair</a> is the oldest and largest in the country. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="List of museums in the United Arab Emirates">list of museums in the United Arab Emirates</a> includes some of regional repute, most famously <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah (city)">Sharjah</a> with its Heritage District containing 17 museums,<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup> which in 1998 was the Cultural Capital of the Arab World.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup> In Dubai, the area of <a href="/wiki/Al_Quoz" title="Al Quoz">Al Quoz</a> has attracted a number of art galleries as well as museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Salsali_Private_Museum" title="Salsali Private Museum">Salsali Private Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup> Abu Dhabi has established a culture district on <a href="/wiki/Saadiyat_Island" title="Saadiyat Island">Saadiyat Island</a>. Six grand projects are planned, including the <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Abu_Dhabi" title="Guggenheim Abu Dhabi">Guggenheim Abu Dhabi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Louvre_Abu_Dhabi" title="Louvre Abu Dhabi">Louvre Abu Dhabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup> Dubai also plans to build a <a href="/wiki/Kunsthal" title="Kunsthal">Kunsthal</a> museum and a district for galleries and artists.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Emirati culture is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Eastern_Arabia" title="Culture of Eastern Arabia">culture of Eastern Arabia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Liwa_(music)" title="Liwa (music)">Liwa</a> is a type of music and dance performed locally, mainly in communities that contain descendants of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> from the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-poetry_361-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poetry-361">[361]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Desert_Rock_Festival" title="Dubai Desert Rock Festival">Dubai Desert Rock Festival</a> is also another major festival consisting of heavy metal and rock artists.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Cinema of the United Arab Emirates">cinema of the United Arab Emirates</a> is minimal but expanding. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emirati_cuisine" title="Emirati cuisine">Emirati cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Luqaimat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luqaimat.jpg/220px-Luqaimat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luqaimat.jpg/330px-Luqaimat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luqaimat.jpg/440px-Luqaimat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1075" data-file-height="1074"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Luqaimat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Arabic_coffee" title="Arabic coffee">Arabic coffee</a> with <a href="/wiki/Lugaimat" class="mw-redirect" title="Lugaimat">Lugaimat</a>; a traditional Emirati sweet.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The traditional food of the Emirates has always been rice, fish and meat. The people of the United Arab Emirates have adopted most of their foods from other West and South Asian countries including Iran, Saudi Arabia, Pakistan, India and Oman. Seafood has been the mainstay of the Emirati diet for centuries. Meat and rice are other staple foods, with <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb and mutton</a> preferred to goat and beef. Popular beverages are coffee and tea, which can be complemented with <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saffron" title="Saffron">saffron</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Spearmint" title="Spearmint">mint</a> to give them a distinctive flavour.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Popular cultural Emirati dishes include <i>threed</i>, <i>machboos</i>, <i>khubisa</i>, <i>khameer</i> and <i>chabab</i> bread among others while <a href="/wiki/Lugaimat" class="mw-redirect" title="Lugaimat">Lugaimat</a> is a famous Emirati dessert. </p>
      <p>With the influence of western culture, fast food has become very popular among young people, to the extent that campaigns have been held to highlight the dangers of fast food excesses.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> Alcohol is allowed to be served only in hotel restaurants and bars. All nightclubs are permitted to sell alcohol. Specific supermarkets may sell alcohol, but these products are sold in separate sections. Likewise, pork, which is <a href="/wiki/Haram" title="Haram">haram</a> (not permitted for Muslims), is sold in separate sections in all major supermarkets. Note that although alcohol may be consumed, it is illegal to be intoxicated in public or drive a motor vehicle with any trace of alcohol in the blood.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Sport in the United Arab Emirates">Sport in the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yas_Marina_Circuit,_October_12,_2018_SkySat_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2542" data-file-height="1430"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yas_Marina_Circuit,_October_12,_2018_SkySat_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Yas_Marina_Circuit" title="Yas Marina Circuit">Yas Marina Circuit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DTC1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/DTC1.jpg/220px-DTC1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/DTC1.jpg/330px-DTC1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/DTC1.jpg/440px-DTC1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="545" data-file-height="409"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DTC1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Tennis_Championships" title="Dubai Tennis Championships">Dubai Tennis Championships</a> in 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> is particularly popular in the United Arab Emirates, and a Grand Prix is annually held at the <a href="/wiki/Yas_Marina_Circuit" title="Yas Marina Circuit">Yas Marina Circuit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yas_Island" title="Yas Island">Yas Island</a> in Abu Dhabi. The race takes place in the evening, and was the first ever Grand Prix to start in daylight and finish at night.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup> Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Camel_racing" title="Camel racing">camel racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falconry" title="Falconry">falconry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endurance_riding" title="Endurance riding">endurance riding</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup> The emirate of <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> is also home to two major <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> courses: the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dubai_Golf_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dubai Golf Club (page does not exist)">Dubai Golf Club</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Golf_Club" title="Emirates Golf Club">Emirates Golf Club</a>. </p>
      <p>In the past, child camel jockeys were used, leading to widespread criticism. Eventually the UAE passed laws banning the use of children for the sport, leading to the prompt removal of almost all child jockeys.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> Recently robot jockeys have been introduced to overcome the problem of child camel jockeys which was an issue of human right violations. <a href="/wiki/Ansar_Burney" title="Ansar Burney">Ansar Burney</a> is often praised for the work he has done in this area.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg/220px-Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg/330px-Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg/440px-Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="798"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Zayed_Sports_City_Stadium" title="Zayed Sports City Stadium">Zayed Sports City Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is a popular sport in the UAE. <a href="/wiki/Al-Nasr_Dubai_SC" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Nasr Dubai SC">Al Nasr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Ain_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Ain Club">Al Ain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Wasl_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Wasl FC">Al Wasl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_FC" title="Sharjah FC">Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Wahda_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Wahda FC">Al Wahda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shabab_Al-Ahli_Dubai_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Shabab Al-Ahli Dubai FC">Shabab Al Ahli</a> are the most popular teams and enjoy the reputation of long-time regional champions.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_Football_Association" title="United Arab Emirates Football Association">United Arab Emirates Football Association</a> was established in 1971 and since then has dedicated its time and effort to promoting the game, organising <a href="/wiki/Youth_program" title="Youth program">youth programmes</a> and improving the abilities of not only its players, but also the officials and coaches involved with its regional teams. The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_football_team" title="United Arab Emirates national football team">UAE</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a>. It was the third consecutive World Cup with two Arab nations qualifying, after <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">Kuwait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> in <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_football_team" title="Iraq national football team">Iraq</a> and Algeria again in <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986</a>. The UAE has won the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Cup of Nations">Gulf Cup Championship</a> twice: the first cup won in January 2007 held in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> and the second in January 2013, held in <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup> The country hosted the <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup">2019 AFC Asian Cup</a>. The UAE team went all the way to the semi-finals, where they were defeated by the eventual champions, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_national_football_team" title="Qatar national football team">Qatar</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is one of the most popular sports in the UAE, largely because of the expatriate population from the <a href="/wiki/SAARC" class="mw-redirect" title="SAARC">SAARC</a> countries, the United Kingdom, and Australia. The <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_Cricket_Association_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah Cricket Association Stadium">Sharjah Cricket Association Stadium</a> in Sharjah has hosted four international <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">test cricket matches</a> so far.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Zayed_Cricket_Stadium" title="Sheikh Zayed Cricket Stadium">Sheikh Zayed Cricket Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> has also hosted <a href="/wiki/International_structure_of_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="International structure of cricket">international cricket</a> matches. Dubai has two cricket stadiums (Dubai <a href="/wiki/Cricket_field" title="Cricket field">Cricket Ground</a> No. 1 and No. 2) with a third, the <a href="/wiki/DSC_Cricket_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="DSC Cricket Stadium">DSC Cricket Stadium</a>, as part of <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Sports_City" title="Dubai Sports City">Dubai Sports City</a>. Dubai is also home to the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[378]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_cricket_team" title="United Arab Emirates national cricket team">UAE national cricket team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996 Cricket World Cup</a> and narrowly missed out on qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a>. They qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2015 Cricket World Cup">2015 Cricket World Cup</a> held in Australia and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[380]</a></sup> UAE has also remained as a 2nd home for the Pakistan Cricket team which couldn't play for about 8 years in its home due to the 2009 terrorist attack against the Sri Lankan cricket team in Lahore. Pakistan played all its home cricket in UAE right from 2009 to 2018 and Pakistan's premier cricket tournament Pakistan Super League was held in UAE for 3-4 editions until Cricket got back to Pakistan in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[381]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup> The 14th edition of the <a href="/wiki/2018_Asia_Cup" title="2018 Asia Cup">Asia Cup</a> Cricket tournament was held in the UAE in September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[383]</a></sup> UAE has also hosted two <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">IPLs</a>. The 7th edition of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a> was held in UAE. The UAE leg hosted 20 matches before moving to India. The <a href="/wiki/2020_Indian_Premier_League" title="2020 Indian Premier League">2020 Indian Premier League</a> was also held in UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Education in the United Arab Emirates">Education in the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityCityHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/UniversityCityHall.jpg/220px-UniversityCityHall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/UniversityCityHall.jpg/330px-UniversityCityHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/UniversityCityHall.jpg/440px-UniversityCityHall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityCityHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>University City Hall is the largest hall located in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_University_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah University City">University City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>. Graduation ceremonies of <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Sharjah" title="American University of Sharjah">American University of Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sharjah" title="University of Sharjah">University of Sharjah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Higher_Colleges_of_Technology" title="Higher Colleges of Technology">Higher Colleges of Technology</a> are notably held here.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_(8582695329).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg/220px-Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg/330px-Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg/440px-Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_(8582695329).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_University" title="Abu Dhabi University">Abu Dhabi University</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education system</a> through secondary level is monitored by the Ministry of Education in all emirates except Abu Dhabi, where it falls under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_Education_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Dhabi Education Council">Abu Dhabi Education Council</a>. It consists of <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle schools</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Schools" class="mw-redirect" title="High Schools">high schools</a>. The public schools are government-funded and the curriculum is created to match the United Arab Emirates' development goals. The medium of instruction in the public school is Arabic with emphasis on English as a second language. There are also many private schools which are internationally accredited. <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public school (government funded)">Public schools</a> in the country are free for citizens of the UAE, while the fees for private schools vary. </p>
      <p>The higher education system is monitored by the Ministry of Higher Education. The ministry also is responsible for admitting students to its <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[385]</a></sup> The adult literacy rate in 2015 was 93.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">[386]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE has shown a strong interest in improving education and research. Enterprises include the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/CERT_Group_of_Companies" title="CERT Group of Companies">CERT</a> Research Centres and the <a href="/wiki/Masdar_Institute_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Masdar Institute of Science and Technology">Masdar Institute of Science and Technology</a> and Institute for Enterprise Development.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup> According to the QS Rankings, the top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_University" title="United Arab Emirates University">United Arab Emirates University</a> (421–430th worldwide), <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_University" title="Khalifa University">Khalifa University</a><sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup> (441–450th worldwide), the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Sharjah" title="American University of Sharjah">American University of Sharjah</a> (431–440th) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sharjah" title="University of Sharjah">University of Sharjah</a> (551–600th worldwide).<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[389]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Demographics of the United Arab Emirates">Demographics of the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg/220px-Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg/330px-Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg/440px-Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="857"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Residential villas in the <a href="/wiki/Palm_Jumeirah" title="Palm Jumeirah">Palm Jumeirah</a> palm fronds in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sharjah,_UAE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg/220px-Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg/330px-Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg/440px-Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sharjah,_UAE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The old residential area in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>, displaying local architecture.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to an estimate by the World Bank, the UAE's population in 2018 stands at 9.543 million. Expatriates and immigrants account for 88.52% while Emiratis make up the remaining 11.48%.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup> This unique imbalance is due to the country's exceptionally high <a href="/wiki/Net_migration_rate" title="Net migration rate">net migration rate</a> of 21.71, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_net_migration_rate" title="List of countries by net migration rate">world's highest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[391]</a></sup> UAE citizenship is very difficult to obtain other than by <a href="/wiki/Filiation" title="Filiation">filiation</a> and only granted under very special circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[392]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UAE is ethnically diverse. The five most populous nationalities in the emirates of Dubai, Sharjah, and Ajman are Indian (25%), Pakistani (12%), Emirati (9%), Bangladeshi (7%), and Filipino (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[393]</a></sup> Expatriates from Europe, Australia, Northern America and Latin America make up 500,000 of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-arabianbusiness.com_394-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabianbusiness.com-394">[394]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">[395]</a></sup> More than 100,000 British nationals live in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[396]</a></sup> The rest of the population are from other <a href="/wiki/Arab_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab World">Arab states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[397]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 88% of the population of the United Arab Emirates is urban.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">[398]</a></sup> The average <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> was 76.7 in 2012, higher than for any other Arab country.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">[399]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uaeinteract2_400-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uaeinteract2-400">[400]</a></sup> With a male/female <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratio</a> of 2.2 males for each female in the total population and 2.75 to 1 for the 15–65 <a href="/wiki/Demographic_profile" title="Demographic profile">age group</a>, the UAE's <a href="/wiki/Gender_mortality_differentials" class="mw-redirect" title="Gender mortality differentials">gender imbalance</a> is second highest in the world after Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[401]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Religion in the United Arab Emirates">Religion in the United Arab Emirates</a>

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the largest and the official <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> of the UAE. The government follows a policy of tolerance toward other religions and rarely interferes in the religious activities of non-Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-404">[404]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are more <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> than <a href="/wiki/Shiite" class="mw-redirect" title="Shiite">Shia</a> Muslims in the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">[405]</a></sup> 85% of the Emirati population are Sunni Muslims. The vast majority of the remainder 15% are Shia Muslims, who are concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Dubai" title="Emirate of Dubai">Emirates of Dubai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Sharjah" title="Emirate of Sharjah">Sharjah</a>. Although no official statistics are available for the breakdown between Sunni and Shia Muslims among noncitizen residents, media estimates suggest less than 20 percent of the noncitizen Muslim population are Shia.<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">[406]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Zayed_Mosque" title="Sheikh Zayed Mosque">Sheikh Zayed Mosque</a> in Abu Dhabi is the largest mosque in the country and a major tourist attraction. <a href="/wiki/Ibadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibadi">Ibadi</a> is common among Omanis in the UAE, while <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> influences exist as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in the United Arab Emirates">Roman Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Protestantism in the United Arab Emirates">Protestants</a> form significant proportions of the Christian minority. The country has at least 45 churches.<sup id="cite_ref-irf127360_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irf127360-407">[407]</a></sup> Many Christians in the United Arab Emirates are of Asian, African, and European origin, along with fellow Middle Eastern countries such as Lebanon, Syria, and Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">[408]</a></sup> The United Arab Emirates forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Vicariate_Apostolic_of_Southern_Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Vicariate Apostolic of Southern Arabia">Apostolic Vicariate of Southern Arabia</a> and the Vicar Apostolic Bishop <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hinder" title="Paul Hinder">Paul Hinder</a> is based in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">[409]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is a small <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> community in the United Arab Emirates. There is only one known <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, which has been open since 2008. The synagogue also welcomes visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[410]</a></sup> As of 2019, according to Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Marc_Schneier" title="Marc Schneier">Marc Schneier</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Foundation_for_Ethnic_Understanding" title="Foundation for Ethnic Understanding">Foundation for Ethnic Understanding</a>, it is estimated that there are about 150 families to 3,000 Jews who live and worship freely in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-Ynt_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ynt-411">[411]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>South Asians in the United Arab Emirates constitute the largest ethnic group in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">[412]</a></sup> Over 2 million Indian migrants (mostly from the southern states of <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanara" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanara">Coastal Karnataka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a>) are estimated to be living in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">[413]</a></sup> There is currently only one Hindu temple in the UAE in Dubai, the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_Temple,_Dubai" title="Hindu Temple, Dubai">Hindu Temple, Dubai</a> (referred to locally as Shiva and Krishna Mandir) located in Dubai. Another temple, the <a href="/wiki/BAPS_Hindu_Mandir_Abu_Dhabi" title="BAPS Hindu Mandir Abu Dhabi">BAPS Hindu Mandir Abu Dhabi</a> is a Hindu temple that is being built by the <a href="/wiki/BAPS_Swaminarayan_Sanstha" class="mw-redirect" title="BAPS Swaminarayan Sanstha">BAPS Swaminarayan Sansthan</a> in Abu Dhabi. </p>
      <p>Other religions also exist in the United Arab Emirates, including <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼís</a> and <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_229-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-229">[229]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> is the national language of the United Arab Emirates. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Arabic" title="Gulf Arabic">Gulf dialect</a> of Arabic is spoken natively by Emirati people.<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">[414]</a></sup> The area was occupied by the British until 1971 and, with many expatriates resident, English is the primary <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> in the UAE. Consequently, a knowledge of English is a requirement when applying for most local jobs. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Health in the United Arab Emirates">Health in the United Arab Emirates</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The life expectancy at birth in the UAE is at 76.96 years.<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">[415]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">Cardiovascular disease</a> is the principal cause of death in the UAE, constituting 28% of total deaths; other major causes are <a href="/wiki/Accident" title="Accident">accidents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Injury" title="Injury">injuries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">malignancies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Congenital_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Congenital disorder">congenital anomalies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_416-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-416">[416]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Body_Mass_Index_(BMI)#WHO_Data_on_Prevalence_of_Obesity_(BMI_above_30)_(2016)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Body Mass Index (BMI)">World Health Organisation data from 2016</a>, 34.5% of adults in the UAE are clinically <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obese</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Body_mass_index" title="Body mass index">body mass index</a> (BMI) score of 30 or more.<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">[417]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2008, the Ministry of Health unveiled a five-year health strategy for the public health sector in the northern emirates, which fall under its purview and which, unlike Abu Dhabi and Dubai, do not have separate healthcare authorities. The strategy focuses on unifying healthcare policy and improving access to healthcare services at reasonable cost, at the same time reducing dependence on overseas treatment. The ministry plans to add three hospitals to the current 14, and 29 primary healthcare centres to the current 86. Nine were scheduled to open in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">[418]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The introduction of mandatory <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a> in Abu Dhabi for <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a> and their dependents was a major driver in reform of healthcare policy. Abu Dhabi nationals were brought under the scheme from 1 June 2008 and Dubai followed for its government employees. Eventually, under federal law, every Emirati and expatriate in the country will be covered by compulsory health insurance under a unified mandatory scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">[419]</a></sup> The country has benefited from medical tourists from all over the <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf</a>. The UAE attracts <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourists</a> seeking <a href="/wiki/Cosmetic_surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Cosmetic surgery">cosmetic surgery</a> and advanced procedures, cardiac and spinal surgery, and dental treatment, as health services have higher standards than other Arab countries in the Persian Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-thenational.ae_420-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenational.ae-420">[420]</a></sup> </p>

The sentence was commuted on appeal to 1 year in prison, followed by deportation. In June 1998, the Shari'a court in Fujairah sentenced three Omani nationals convicted of robbery to have their right hands amputated. The Fujairah prosecutor's office instead commuted the sentence to a term of imprisonment.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=United+Arab+Emirates+%E2%80%93+Country+Reports+on+Human+Rights+Practices&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2F2009-2017.state.gov%2Fj%2Fdrl%2Frls%2Fhrrpt%2F2000%2Fnea%2F824.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnited+Arab+Emirates" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
